## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the time derivative of species concentration, which is the fundamental differential form of reaction rate laws. The relationship typically expresses the rate as a function of concentration raised to an order-dependent power, potentially modulated by time-dependent factors like catalyst deactivation or diffusion limitations.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant reaction rate independent of concentration)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate linearly proportional to concentration)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- General nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical power-law concentration dependence)
- Reversible first-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * (A - c1) (net rate approaching equilibrium concentration)
- Autocatalytic rate equation: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + A) (product enhances reaction rate, sigmoidal progress)
- Catalyst deactivation model: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent rate constant decay or activation)
- Diffusion-controlled consumption: dA_dt = c0 * A * t**(-0.5) (Noyes-Winterbottom kinetics, rate slows as sqrt(time))
- Delayed onset kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * c1 * t / (c2 + t) (induction period before full rate develops)
- Consecutive reaction net rate: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (balance between linear formation and quadratic consumption)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order identification → Rate scales as A**n; integer n indicates elementary steps, fractional n suggests complex/multistep mechanisms.
- Equilibrium approach → Linear driving force term (A - c1) or sign reversal near constant A, indicating reversible kinetics.
- Autocatalytic inflection → Rate initially rises with A before declining, mathematically captured by A*(c + A) creating an inflection point in concentration profiles.
- Diffusion-limited regime → Rate decays as t**(-0.5), reflecting diminishing concentration gradients and boundary layer growth over time.
- Catalyst deactivation/aging → Multiplicative time-dependent factor exp(c*t) or t**c modulating the base rate constant downward.
- Zero-order plateau → Constant rate dA_dt ≈ c0 over extended A range, typical of surface-saturated or enzyme-saturated systems.
- Induction/lag phase → Rate suppressed at low t, often modeled by rational or exponential time factors multiplying the concentration term.

### Step-by-Step Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) function is:
`GT(A) = -0.772588*A**2 - 0.772588*A + 0.740207*cos(log(A + 1))`
This is a quadratic polynomial in `A` plus a cosine-of-logarithm term. Any matching candidate must be able to represent exactly `a*A**2 + b*A + d*cos(log(A + 1))` (or an equivalent phase-shifted sine form) by adjusting its free constants. Basis functions like `exp(A)`, `sin(A)`, `log(A)`, or fractional powers cannot algebraically transform into `cos(log(A+1))` or `A**2`.

**Candidate 1:** `A*(A*c0 + c1) + c2*exp(A*c3) + c4*log(c5*sin(A*c6 + c7) + 1)`
Contains `exp(A)` and `log(sin(A))`. Lacks `cos(log(A+1))`. `[NO MATCH]`

**Candidate 2:** `(c0 + (A*c1 + 1)*(A*(A*c2 + c3) + c4*exp(A*c5)))/(A*c1 + 1)`
Simplifies to `c0/(A*c1+1) + c2*A**2 + c3*A + c4*exp(c5*A)`. Contains `exp(A)`. `[NO MATCH]`

**Candidate 3:** `A*(A*c0 + c1) + c2*exp(A*c3) + c4*log(A*c5 + 1)`
Contains `exp(A)` and `log(A)`. Lacks `cos(log(A+1))`. `[NO MATCH]`

**Candidate 4:** `A*(A*c0 + c1) + c2*exp(A*c3) + c4*exp(c5*sin(A*c6 + c7))`
